I feel like up until 7th grade, I had a strong Indian accent. I don’t think I really had a command of the English language perfectly until like 8th grade. There were just things I didn’t know. I felt so different from other kids. Even though I went to a pretty diverse school, most of my friends weren’t Indian. It was really weird growing up because home would be super Indian and then school would be super American. In the evening, all my parents would watch were Indian TV shows, and when we went to see movies they were Indian, too. The first American movie I watched was “Harry Potter,” and I started crying and had to leave the theater. So they really only took us to Indian movies.\" Did you feel comfortable telling your friends about Indian culture? \"Not at all. Even if I did mention it, they'd immediately tune out if I talked about my culture, so I sort of learned it's not worth talking about it, sometimes. But I like being Indian. The traditions, the community--it’s really cool that even with different languages or religions, we can still unite around traditions, like everyone coming out for Holi. It’s a part of our upbringing we can all resonate with.\" -------FAST FACTS------- Life choices your parents don’t approve of? Dating. Partying. Basically, anything that involves having fun. Favorite memory? Going to Garba every year growing up. My mom loves it so much and its fun to do it with my family and now, too. Favorite Indian food?
